  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c9dff764-919a-4201-82d3-90178d18b137'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText973977412037744419" style="display:none">New York, sommet de l’Empire State Building, 23 heures <br />Nathan, regardez le garçon à l’anorak orange <br />- Pardon ? <br />- Regardez le garçon à l’anorak orange <br />- Bon sang, Garrett, pourquoi voulez-vous que je regarde ? <br />- Parce qu’il va mourir. <br />Moins d’une minute plus tard, l’adolescent se tire une balle dans la tête. Et c’est ainsi que Nathan Del Amico, brillant avocat new-yorkais, découvre l’étrange pouvoir de Garrett Goodrich. <br />A la fois choqué et abasourdi, Nathan voudrait chasser cette scène de son esprit… <br />Alors qui est ce Garrett Goodrich ? Un cancérologue chevronné, directeur d’un important centre de soins palliatifs. Il n’a rien d’un illuminé et pourtant il se dit capable de prévoir la mort. Il prétend avoir une « mission » : accompagner ceux qui vont mourir jusqu’aux frontières de l’Autre Monde pour qu’ils quittent la vie en paix avec eux-mêmes</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1273611368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273611368" />
    <a title="Helynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1361138-helynne"><img alt="Helynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442489921p2/1361138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273611368?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helynne" href="/user/show/1361138-helynne">Helynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273611368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15877976254612790902">Those who remember the TV series <i>The Twilight Zone,</i>, may recall a particularly creepy episode called “The Purple Testament” in which an American GI in World War II Europe has the unenviable gift of knowing who is about to die. He can see a bright light come over the faces of a wounded man in the hospital or an officer preparing for battle, and sure enough, both die quickly. As the program ends, the soldier sees the light come over his own face in the mirror as well as over the face of the driver</span>
  <span id="freeText15877976254612790902" style="display:none">Those who remember the TV series <i>The Twilight Zone,</i>, may recall a particularly creepy episode called “The Purple Testament” in which an American GI in World War II Europe has the unenviable gift of knowing who is about to die. He can see a bright light come over the faces of a wounded man in the hospital or an officer preparing for battle, and sure enough, both die quickly. As the program ends, the soldier sees the light come over his own face in the mirror as well as over the face of the driver of a jeep he is about to get into. You can guess the outcome. I wonder if this episode may have inspired Guillaume Musso, a French novelist who has spent time in New York. His French-language novel from 2004 involves a rich, successful New York attorney Nathan Del Amico, who is approached by Garrett Goodrich, a doctor who claims to be a Messenger; that is, a person who sees a light flash over certain people’s faces, and knows they are scheduled for imminent demise. At first, Nathan, an agnostic and an intellectual, thinks this is crap, but some very traumatic experiences with specific people eventually convince him that Goodrich is what he says he is. This leads Nathan to assume that he himself will be the next one to die, a belief that is particularly troubling for a man of 30 who has a small daughter and who is still in love with his ex-wife . Nathan also wonders if Goodrich’s visit has something to do with the fact that Nathan once had a near-death experience as an eight-year-old child. Indeed there is a connection, but not the one that we might have imagined, and which leads to an unexpected twist at the end. Not exactly a thriller or a mystery, this novel is still compelling and thought provoking, and gets readers thinking about integrity, priorities, misplaced values, and of course, <i> carpe diem.</i> The plot gets a little convoluted toward the end as it delves more into Nathan and his mother’s backgrounds and his rocky relationship with his in-laws, then a hit-run accident, and a blackmail threat. The English-language film version leaves most of this out, and the simplification is for the better, in my opinion. The 2008 film stars John Malkovich as the Messenger (although his name is changed to Dr. Joseph Kay) and popular French actor Romain Duris as Nathan. Of course, with his very noticeable French accent, Duris portrays Nathan as a French guy who has somehow become a New York lawyer (and why not?) instead of the native New Yorker he is in the book. Actually, I think the choice of Duris was more of an homage to the French origins of the novel, and he has a good grasp of the role.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15877976254612790902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer6943686183212256056">While I enjoyed reading this book, there were a few issues that weren't to my liking. For starters, I was surprised that the book was set in New York. I knew that Guillaume Musso is a contemporary French author and I was expecting the book to be set in France. That was disappointing to me (but that's just me and only because I have a somewhat complicated history with New York). Second of all, there are things in the novel that didn't quite make sense. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ here are some examples: when</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6943686183212256056" style="display:none">While I enjoyed reading this book, there were a few issues that weren't to my liking. For starters, I was surprised that the book was set in New York. I knew that Guillaume Musso is a contemporary French author and I was expecting the book to be set in France. That was disappointing to me (but that's just me and only because I have a somewhat complicated history with New York). Second of all, there are things in the novel that didn't quite make sense. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ here are some examples: when Nathan goes to California to pick up his daughter, he realizes that he must try to win his ex-wife again, so he sends his daughter to New York with practically a stranger, someone he met only recently. Then, when he goes back to his ex-wife's house, she never even asks where their daughter is and why Nathan came back from the airport alone. Huh? Another one comes to mind, towards the end of the novel: when Nathan sees kind of a halo around his ex-wife's head, he instantly realizes that it means she will die soon and that it means that he is a messenger, yet, never in the book was it ever discussed that a messenger can <b>see</b> something. Also, Nathan decides to sacrifice himself and take blame for a car crash that injured a 7-year old boy. A big deal is made that Nathan's father in law will represent him, but yet the entire thing is dropped from the story line and we don't get any resolution in that  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13205559573227099009">I can always count on Mr. Guillaume Musso to put me in a better mood and lift my spirit. This is the third book I read written by him and I really enjoyed it. His books have a common denominator - the plots are very original and sometimes a bit fantasy-like, they are read very quickly, the writing is very basic, more like a movie script, but throughout the book and in the end you are left with a warm and bitter sweet feeling. This one was no exception - I read it yesterday in one sitting and kee</span>
  <span id="freeText13205559573227099009" style="display:none">I can always count on Mr. Guillaume Musso to put me in a better mood and lift my spirit. This is the third book I read written by him and I really enjoyed it. His books have a common denominator - the plots are very original and sometimes a bit fantasy-like, they are read very quickly, the writing is very basic, more like a movie script, but throughout the book and in the end you are left with a warm and bitter sweet feeling. This one was no exception - I read it yesterday in one sitting and keep thinking about it today. I recommend it as long as you don't expect an eloquently-written literary masterpiece - somehow his books always manage to touch my heart and that counts for something!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1724337621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8082565097580440752">The amazing story of Nathan del Amico, a prominent lawyer of New York, how he deals with the upcoming and important changes in his successful life; death. I don't want to give any spoiler; all the book is filled up with surprises. <br/><br/>This is the first book I read in french and every single page was worth it, I couldn't stop turning each page. I completely recommend this book, you will love each character and the story from beginning to end.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8W4PVej897/8zEDDF4E6oHcPCGBABmcWdhlRzFRbFqoYSA9uwXcb/2AWjjVtcPw+cJiqvO1uSyxehoy9ggbeWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IGCH49E/S00GAsGeCY9e8ZYFuP04UGxK+Fa1Xh/q5VLJRofY+LSnDZrYD2hzfphvkZIaIZU4QHDQyWgvybctow==')})
  }

J\'ai souri, je comprenais très bien de quoi elle parlait. » Et si l\'enfant que vous étiez rencontrait l\'adulte que vous êtes devenu... Drôle et tendre, Le Voleur d\'ombres est le onzième roman de Marc Levy. عن دار النشر الإيطالية فلترينيللي وهي أحدى أكبر دور النشر الإيطالية وأعرقها. وفي غضون شهور قليلة باعت أكثر من مائة ألف نسخة في ظاهرة غريبة عن حركة بيع الكتاب في إيطالية.\nثم حازت الرواية على جوائز أدبية قيّمة من أهمها جائزة &quot;كارلو ليفي&quot; الأدبية وجائزة &quot;لو ستريغا&quot;، أهم وأعرق جائزة أدبية في إيطالية، للأدباء الشباب. وسريعًا ترجمت الرواية إلى كل اللغات الأوروبية، وحصلت على ثناء ملحوظ في الأوساط الثقافية الأمريكية، وحاليًا جاري العمل لتحويلها إلى فيلم سينمائي.\n&quot;نجح كاتوتسيلا في دعوتنا إلى مشاركة هذه المشاعر الحميمة بشروط قاسية ومجهولة. أثار في ضمائرنا أهمية السرد في اقتسام الحلم والكابوس. هذا هو النمط الأدبي الذي أرى أنه قادر على قصّ الملحمة الكبرى التي نعيش يومياتها المعاصرة: اللجوء والهجرة والبحر المتوسط&quot;.\nالروائي الإيطالي الشهير إرّي دي لوكا\n&quot;استطاع الكاتب أن يوثق قصة حقيقية ليس بوسع الخيال أن يبتدع مثلها. وأغمنا التشويق في صفحاتها على حبس أنفاسنا والشعور بأننا نتحمل جزءًا من المسؤولية لما يقع من كوارث في الجانب الآخر من العالم&quot;.\nالروائي الإيطالي روبرتو سافيانو مؤلف رواية غومورا.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"15250131138952164022\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14959602392565365473">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. H</span>
  <span id="freeText14959602392565365473" style="display:none">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. He came home to France with his head filled with ideas for novels. The readers can easily see the influence his time in the United States has had on him, as the action in his books takes place overseas. He currently teaches in a high school in the south of France, all the while working on his novels. His first published novel was with Editions Anne Carriere in 2001: <i>Skidamarink</i>, this novel did not reach out to the masses however, but his following novels published on XO Editions have all been hugely successful, some of them translated into 20 languages. His novel, <i>Afterwards</i>, has been adapted to the big screen and was in cinemas January 2009, starring John Malkovich, Evangeline Lily and Romain Duris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14959602392565365473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
